<p><b>Blender</b> is a professional <a href="/wiki/Free_and_open-source_software" title="Free and open-source software">free and open-source</a> <a href="/wiki/3D_computer_graphics_software" title="3D computer graphics software">3D computer graphics software</a> product used for creating <a href="/wiki/Animation" title="Animation">animated films</a>, <a href="/wiki/Visual_effects" title="Visual effects">visual effects</a>, art, <a href="/wiki/3D_printing" title="3D printing">3D printed</a> models, interactive 3D applications and <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video games</a>. Blender's features include <a href="/wiki/3D_modeling" title="3D modeling">3D modeling</a>, <a href="/wiki/UV_mapping" title="UV mapping">UV unwrapping</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texture_mapping" title="Texture mapping">texturing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raster_graphics_editor" title="Raster graphics editor">raster graphics editing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skeletal_animation" title="Skeletal animation">rigging and skinning</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fluid_simulation" title="Fluid simulation">fluid and smoke simulation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Particle_system" title="Particle system">particle</a> simulation, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soft_body_dynamics" title="Soft body dynamics">soft body</a> simulation, <a href="/wiki/Digital_sculpting" title="Digital sculpting">sculpting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer_animation" title="Computer animation">animating</a>, <a href="/wiki/Match_moving" title="Match moving">match moving</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Camera_tracking" title="Camera tracking">camera tracking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rendering_(computer_graphics)" title="Rendering (computer graphics)">rendering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Video_editing_software" title="Video editing software">video editing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Compositing" title="Compositing">compositing</a>. It further features an integrated <a href="/wiki/Blender_Game_Engine" title="Blender Game Engine">game engine</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blender-Desktop-2-77.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1029" data-file-width="1919" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Blender-Desktop-2-77.png/250px-Blender-Desktop-2-77.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Blender-Desktop-2-77.png/375px-Blender-Desktop-2-77.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Blender-Desktop-2-77.png/500px-Blender-Desktop-2-77.png 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Blender-Desktop-2-77.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The desktop scene in version 2.77</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> animation studio <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Neo_Geo_(animation_studio)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Neo Geo (animation studio) (page does not exist)">Neo Geo</a> developed Blender as an in-house application in January 1995,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> with the primary author being software developer <a href="/wiki/Ton_Roosendaal" title="Ton Roosendaal">Ton Roosendaal</a>. The name <i>Blender</i> was inspired by a song by <a href="/wiki/Yello" title="Yello">Yello</a>, from the album <i><a href="/wiki/Baby_(Yello_album)" title="Baby (Yello album)">Baby</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> When Neo Geo was acquired by another company, Ton Roosendaal and Frank van Beek founded <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Not_a_Number_Technologies&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Not a Number Technologies (page does not exist)">Not a Number Technologies</a> (NaN) in June 1998 to further develop Blender, initially distributing it as <a href="/wiki/Shareware" title="Shareware">shareware</a> until NaN went bankrupt in 2002.</p>
<p>On July 18, 2002, Roosendaal started the <i>"Free Blender"</i> campaign, a <a href="/wiki/Crowdfunding" title="Crowdfunding">crowdfunding</a> precursor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The campaign aimed for <a href="/wiki/Open-source_software" title="Open-source software">open-sourcing</a> Blender for a one-time payment of €100,000 (US$100,670 at the time) collected from the community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> On September 7, 2002, it was announced that they had collected enough funds and would release the Blender <a href="/wiki/Source_code" title="Source code">source code</a>. Today, Blender is <a href="/wiki/Free_software" title="Free software">free</a>, open-source software that is—apart from the Blender Institute's two full-time and two part-time employees—developed by the community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Blender_Foundation" title="Blender Foundation">Blender Foundation</a> initially reserved the right to use <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dual_license" title="Dual license">dual licensing</a>, so that, in addition to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GPLv2" title="GPLv2">GPLv2</a>, Blender would have been available also under the <i>Blender License</i> that did not require disclosing source code but required payments to the Blender Foundation. However, they never exercised this option and suspended it indefinitely in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Blender is solely available under "GNU GPLv2 or any later" and was not updated to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GPLv3" title="GPLv3">GPLv3</a>, as "no evident benefits" were seen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-libredwg-gplv3-opinion_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-libredwg-gplv3-opinion-12">[12]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Suzanne">Suzanne</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Suzanne">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Suzanne.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="200" data-file-width="240" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Suzanne.svg/220px-Suzanne.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Suzanne.svg/330px-Suzanne.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Suzanne.svg/440px-Suzanne.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Suzanne.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Suzanne</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In January–February 2002 it was clear that NaN could not survive and would close the doors in March. Nevertheless, they put out one more release, 2.25. As a sort-of <a href="/wiki/Easter_egg_(media)" title="Easter egg (media)">easter egg</a>, a last personal tag, the artists and developers decided to add a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3D_model" title="3D model">3D model</a> of a <a href="/wiki/Chimpanzee" title="Chimpanzee">chimpanzee</a> head. It was created by Willem-Paul van Overbruggen (SLiD3), who named it <b>Suzanne</b> after the orangutan in the <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Smith" title="Kevin Smith">Kevin Smith</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Jay_and_Silent_Bob_Strike_Back" title="Jay and Silent Bob Strike Back">Jay and Silent Bob Strike Back</a></i>.</p>
<p>Suzanne is Blender's alternative to more common <a href="/wiki/List_of_common_3D_test_models" title="List of common 3D test models">test models</a> such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Utah_Teapot" title="Utah Teapot">Utah Teapot</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stanford_Bunny" title="Stanford Bunny">Stanford Bunny</a>. A low-polygon model with only 500 faces, Suzanne is often used as a quick and easy way to test material, animation, rigs, texture, and lighting setups and is also frequently used in joke images.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Suzanne is still included in Blender. The largest Blender contest gives out an award called the <a href="/wiki/Suzanne_Award" title="Suzanne Award">Suzanne Award</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Clones">Clones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Clones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Due to Blender's open source nature, other programs have tried to take advantage of its success by repackaging and selling cosmetically-modified versions of it. Examples include IllusionMage, 3DMofun and Fluid Designer,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> the latter recognized as Blender-based.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Features">Features</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Features">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Steps_of_forensic_facial_reconstruction_-_Virtual_Mummy_-_cogitas3d.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="480" height="300" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Steps_of_forensic_facial_reconstruction_-_Virtual_Mummy_-_cogitas3d.gif/300px-Steps_of_forensic_facial_reconstruction_-_Virtual_Mummy_-_cogitas3d.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Steps_of_forensic_facial_reconstruction_-_Virtual_Mummy_-_cogitas3d.gif/450px-Steps_of_forensic_facial_reconstruction_-_Virtual_Mummy_-_cogitas3d.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cc/Steps_of_forensic_facial_reconstruction_-_Virtual_Mummy_-_cogitas3d.gif 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Steps_of_forensic_facial_reconstruction_-_Virtual_Mummy_-_cogitas3d.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Steps of forensic facial reconstruction of a mummy made on Blender by the Brazilian 3D designer <a href="/wiki/C%C3%ADcero_Moraes" title="Cícero Moraes">Cícero Moraes</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Official releases of Blender for <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a>, <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">MacOS</a></span> and <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-download_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-download-26">[26]</a></sup> as well as a <a href="/wiki/Porting" title="Porting">port</a> for <a href="/wiki/FreeBSD" title="FreeBSD">FreeBSD</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> are available in both <a href="/wiki/32-bit" title="32-bit">32-bit</a> and <a href="/wiki/64-bit_computing" title="64-bit computing">64-bit</a> versions. Though it is often distributed without extensive example scenes found in some other programs,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> the software contains features that are characteristic of high-end 3D software. Among its capabilities are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Support for a variety of geometric primitives, including <a href="/wiki/Polygon_mesh" title="Polygon mesh">polygon meshes</a>, fast <a href="/wiki/Subdivision_surface" title="Subdivision surface">subdivision surface</a> modeling, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bezier_curve" title="Bezier curve">Bezier curves</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nonuniform_rational_B-spline" title="Nonuniform rational B-spline">NURBS surfaces</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metaballs" title="Metaballs">metaballs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Icosphere" title="Icosphere">icospheres</a>, multi-res <a href="/wiki/Digital_sculpting" title="Digital sculpting">digital sculpting</a> (including dynamic topology, maps baking, remeshing, resymetrize, decimation), outline <a href="/wiki/Font" title="Font">font</a>, and a new n-gon modeling system called B-mesh.</li>
<li>Internal render engine with <a href="/wiki/Scanline_rendering" title="Scanline rendering">scanline rendering</a>, indirect lighting, and ambient occlusion that can export in a wide variety of formats.</li>
<li>A <a href="/wiki/Path_tracing" title="Path tracing">pathtracer</a> render engine called Cycles, which can take advantage of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GPU" title="GPU">GPU</a> for rendering. Cycles supports the <a href="/wiki/Open_Shading_Language" title="Open Shading Language">Open Shading Language</a> since Blender 2.65.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>Integration with a number of external render engines through plugins.</li>
<li>Keyframed animation tools including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inverse_kinematic_animation" title="Inverse kinematic animation">inverse kinematics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skeletal_animation" title="Skeletal animation">armature (skeletal)</a>, hook, curve and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lattice-based_deformation" title="Lattice-based deformation">lattice-based deformations</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shape_animation" title="Shape animation">shape animations</a>, non-linear animation, constraints, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vertex_weighting" title="Vertex weighting">vertex weighting</a>.</li>
<li>Simulation tools for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soft_body_dynamics" title="Soft body dynamics">soft body dynamics</a> including mesh <a href="/wiki/Collision_detection" title="Collision detection">collision detection</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lattice_Boltzmann_methods" title="Lattice Boltzmann methods">LBM</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fluid_dynamic" title="Fluid dynamic">fluid dynamics</a>, smoke simulation, <a href="/wiki/Bullet_(software)" title="Bullet (software)">Bullet</a> <a href="/wiki/Rigid_body_dynamics" title="Rigid body dynamics">rigid body dynamics</a>, ocean generator with waves.</li>
<li>A particle system that includes support for particle-based hair.</li>
<li>Modifiers to apply non-destructive effects.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a> scripting for tool creation and prototyping, game logic, importing/exporting from other formats, task automation and custom tools.</li>
<li>Basic non-linear video/audio editing.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Blender_Game_Engine" title="Blender Game Engine">Blender Game Engine</a>, a sub-project, offers interactivity features such as <a href="/wiki/Collision_detection" title="Collision detection">collision detection</a>, dynamics engine, and programmable logic. It also allows the creation of stand-alone, real-time applications ranging from architectural visualization to <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video games</a>.</li>
<li>A fully integrated node-based compositor within the rendering pipeline accelerated with <a href="/wiki/OpenCL" title="OpenCL">OpenCL</a>.</li>
<li>Procedural and node-based textures, as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3D_paint_tool" title="3D paint tool">texture painting</a>, projective painting, <a href="/wiki/Vertex_painting" title="Vertex painting">vertex painting</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weight_map_painting" title="Weight map painting">weight painting</a> and dynamic painting.</li>
<li>Real-time control during physics simulation and rendering.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Camera_tracking" title="Camera tracking">Camera and object tracking</a>.</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="User_interface">User interface</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: User interface">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blender_Version_2.570.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1366" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Blender_Version_2.570.jpg/300px-Blender_Version_2.570.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Blender_Version_2.570.jpg/450px-Blender_Version_2.570.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Blender_Version_2.570.jpg/600px-Blender_Version_2.570.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Blender_Version_2.570.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Blender's user interface underwent a significant update during the 2.5x series</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Blender's <a href="/wiki/User_interface" title="User interface">user interface</a> incorporates the following concepts:</p>
<dl>
<dt>Editing modes</dt>
<dd>The two primary modes of work are <i>Object Mode</i> and <i>Edit Mode</i>, which are toggled with the <tt>Tab</tt> key. Object mode is used to manipulate individual objects as a unit, while Edit mode is used to manipulate the actual object data. For example, Object Mode can be used to move, scale, and rotate entire <a href="/wiki/Polygon_mesh" title="Polygon mesh">polygon meshes</a>, and Edit Mode can be used to manipulate the individual vertices of a single mesh. There are also several other modes, such as Vertex Paint, Weight Paint, and Sculpt Mode.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hotkey" title="Hotkey">Hotkey</a> usage</dt>
<dd>Most of the commands are accessible via <a href="/wiki/Keyboard_shortcut" title="Keyboard shortcut">hotkeys</a>. There are also comprehensive <a href="/wiki/Graphical_user_interface" title="Graphical user interface">GUI</a> menus.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>Numeric input</dt>
<dd>Numeric buttons can be "dragged" to change their value directly without the need to aim at a particular widget, as well as being set using the keyboard. Both sliders and number buttons can be constrained to various step sizes with modifiers like the <tt>Ctrl</tt> and <tt>Shift</tt> keys. <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a> expressions can also be typed directly into number entry fields, allowing mathematical expressions to specify values.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dt>Workspace management</dt>
<dd>The Blender GUI builds its own <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiled_windowing_system" title="Tiled windowing system">tiled windowing system</a> on top of one or multiple windows provided by the underlying platform. One platform window (often sized to fill the screen) is divided into sections and subsections that can be of any type of Blender's views or window-types. The user can define multiple layouts of such Blender windows, called <i>screens</i>, and switch quickly between them by selecting from a menu or with keyboard shortcuts. Each window-type's own GUI elements can be controlled with the same tools that manipulate 3D view. For example, one can zoom in and out of GUI-buttons using similar controls one zooms in and out in the 3D viewport. The GUI viewport and screen layout is fully user-customizable. It is possible to set up the interface for specific tasks such as video editing or <a href="/wiki/UV_mapping" title="UV mapping">UV mapping</a> or texturing by hiding features not used for the task.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hardware_requirements">Hardware requirements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Hardware requirements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Supported_platforms">Supported platforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Supported platforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Blender is available for Windows Vista and above, Mac OSX 10.6 and above, and Linux. Blender 2.76b is the last supported release for Windows XP. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-system-requirements_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-system-requirements-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="File_format">File format</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: File format">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Blender features an internal file system that can pack multiple scenes into a single file (called a "<b>.blend</b>" file).</p>
<ul>
<li>All of Blender's ".blend" files are forward, backward, and cross-platform compatible with other versions of Blender, with the following exceptions:
<ul>
<li>Loading animations stored in post-2.5 files in Blender pre-2.5. This is due to the reworked animation subsystem introduced in Blender 2.5 being inherently incompatible with older versions.</li>
<li>Loading meshes stored in post 2.63. This is due to the introduction of BMesh, a more versatile mesh format.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>All scenes, objects, materials, textures, sounds, images, post-production effects for an entire animation can be stored in a single ".blend" file. Data loaded from external sources, such as images and sounds, can also be stored externally and referenced through either an absolute or relative pathname. Likewise, ".blend" files themselves can also be used as libraries of Blender assets.</li>
<li>Interface configurations are retained in the ".blend" files.</li>
</ul>
<p>A wide variety of import/export scripts that extend Blender capabilities (accessing the object data via an internal <a href="/wiki/Application_programming_interface" title="Application programming interface">API</a>) make it possible to inter-operate with other 3D tools.</p>
<p>Blender organizes data as various kinds of "data blocks", such as Objects, Meshes, Lamps, Scenes, Materials, Images and so on. An object in Blender consists of multiple data blocks – for example, what the user would describe as a polygon mesh consists of at least an Object and a Mesh data block, and usually also a Material and many more, linked together. This allows various data blocks to refer to each other. There may be, for example, multiple Objects that refer to the same Mesh, and making subsequent editing of the shared mesh result in shape changes in all Objects using this Mesh. Objects, meshes, materials, textures etc. can also be linked to from other .blend files, which is what allows the use of .blend files as reusable resource libraries.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_editing">Video editing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Video editing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blender_VSE_2.73a.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1366" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Blender_VSE_2.73a.png/250px-Blender_VSE_2.73a.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Blender_VSE_2.73a.png/375px-Blender_VSE_2.73a.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Blender_VSE_2.73a.png/500px-Blender_VSE_2.73a.png 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Blender_VSE_2.73a.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Video Editor (VSE)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Blender features a fully functional, production ready Non-Linear video editor called Video Sequence Editor or VSE for short. Blender's VSE has many features including effects like <a href="/wiki/Gaussian_blur" title="Gaussian blur">Gaussian Blur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Color_grading" title="Color grading">color grading</a>, Fade and Wipe transitions, and other video transformations. However, there is no multi-core support for rendering video with VSE.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="WebGL_authoring">WebGL authoring</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: WebGL authoring">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Blend4Web" title="Blend4Web">Blend4Web</a>, an open source <a href="/wiki/WebGL" title="WebGL">WebGL</a> framework, can be used to convert whole Blender scenes with graphics, animation, sound and physics to work in standard web browsers. Export can be performed with a single click, even as a standalone web page.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blend4web_about_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-blend4web_about-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rendering_and_ray_tracing">Rendering and ray tracing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Rendering and ray tracing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Cycles is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Path_Tracing" title="Path Tracing">path-tracing</a> <a href="/wiki/Rendering_(computer_graphics)" title="Rendering (computer graphics)">render engine</a> that is designed to be interactive and easy to use, while still supporting many production features.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual-cycles-intro_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-manual-cycles-intro-33">[33]</a></sup> It comes installed as an add-on that is available by default and can be activated in the top header.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="GPU_rendering">GPU rendering</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: GPU rendering">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cycles supports <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GPU" title="GPU">GPU</a> rendering which is used to help speed up rendering times. There are two GPU rendering modes: <a href="/wiki/CUDA" title="CUDA">CUDA</a>, which is the preferred method for <a href="/wiki/Nvidia" title="Nvidia">NVIDIA</a> graphics cards; and <a href="/wiki/OpenCL" title="OpenCL">OpenCL</a>, which supports rendering on <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Micro_Devices" title="Advanced Micro Devices">AMD</a> graphics cards. Multiple GPUs are also supported, which can be used to create a <a href="/wiki/Render_farm" title="Render farm">render farm</a> – although having multiple GPUs doesn't increase the available memory because each GPU can only access its own memory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Integrator">Integrator</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Integrator">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The integrator is the rendering algorithm used for lighting computations. Cycles currently supports a path tracing integrator with direct light sampling. It works well for various lighting setups, but is not as suitable for <a href="/wiki/Caustic_(optics)" title="Caustic (optics)">caustics</a> and some other complex lighting situations. Rays are traced from the camera into the scene, bouncing around until they find a light source such as a lamp, an object emitting light, or the world background. To find lamps and surfaces emitting light, both indirect light sampling (letting the ray follow the surface <a href="/wiki/Bidirectional_scattering_distribution_function" title="Bidirectional scattering distribution function">BSDF</a>) and direct light sampling (picking a light source and tracing a ray towards it) are used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are two types of integrators:</p>
<ol>
<li>The default path tracing integrator is a pure path tracer. At each hit it bounces light in one direction and picks one light to receive lighting from. This makes each individual sample faster to compute, but typically requires more samples to clean up the noise.</li>
<li>The alternative is a branched path tracing integrator which at the first hit splits the path for different surface components and takes all lights into account for shading instead of just one. This makes each sample slower, but reduces noise, especially in scenes dominated by direct or one-bounce lighting.</li>
</ol>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Open_Shading_Language">Open Shading Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Open Shading Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Blender users can create their own nodes using the <a href="/wiki/Open_Shading_Language" title="Open Shading Language">Open Shading Language</a> although it is important to note that there is no support for it on GPUs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Materials">Materials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Materials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Materials define the look of <a href="/wiki/Polygon_mesh" title="Polygon mesh">meshes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Non-uniform_rational_B-spline" title="Non-uniform rational B-spline">NURBS curves</a> and other geometric objects. They consist of three <a href="/wiki/Shader" title="Shader">shaders</a>, defining the mesh's appearance of the surface, volume inside, and displacement of the surface.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual-cycles-intro_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-manual-cycles-intro-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Surface_shader">Surface shader</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Surface shader">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The surface shader defines the light interaction at the surface of the mesh. One or more <a href="/wiki/Bidirectional_scattering_distribution_function" title="Bidirectional scattering distribution function">BSDFs</a> can specify if incoming light is reflected back, refracted into the mesh, or absorbed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual-cycles-intro_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-manual-cycles-intro-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Volume_shader">Volume shader</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Volume shader">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>When the surface shader does not reflect or absorb light, it enters the volume. If no volume shader is specified, it will pass straight through to the other side of the mesh.</p>
<p>If one is defined, a volume shader describes the light interaction as it passes through the volume of the mesh. Light may be scattered, absorbed, or emitted at any point in the volume.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual-cycles-intro_33-3"><a href="#cite_note-manual-cycles-intro-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Displacement_shader">Displacement shader</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Displacement shader">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The shape of the surface may be altered by displacement shaders. This way, <a href="/wiki/Texture_mapping" title="Texture mapping">textures</a> can be used to make the mesh surface more detailed.</p>
<p>Depending on the settings, the displacement may be virtual, only modifying the surface normals to give the impression of displacement (also known as <a href="/wiki/Bump_mapping" title="Bump mapping">bump mapping</a>) or a combination of real and virtual displacement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual-cycles-intro_33-4"><a href="#cite_note-manual-cycles-intro-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demo_reels">Demo reels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Demo reels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Blender website contains several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Showreel_(actors)" title="Showreel (actors)">demo reels</a> that showcase various features of Blender.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Physics">Physics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Physics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Blender can be used to simulate smoke, rain, dust, cloth, water, hair and rigid bodies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cloth_simulation">Cloth simulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Cloth simulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

</div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Cloth_modeling" title="Cloth modeling">cloth</a> is any piece of mesh that has been designated as 'cloth' in the physics tab.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fluid_simulation">Fluid simulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Fluid simulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Physics-Fluid-Simulation-Blender.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="280" data-file-width="412" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Physics-Fluid-Simulation-Blender.gif/220px-Physics-Fluid-Simulation-Blender.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Physics-Fluid-Simulation-Blender.gif/330px-Physics-Fluid-Simulation-Blender.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1c/Physics-Fluid-Simulation-Blender.gif 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Physics-Fluid-Simulation-Blender.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Physics fluid simulation</div>
</div>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Physics_Fluid_Simulation">Physics Fluid Simulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Physics Fluid Simulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fluid_simulation" title="Fluid simulation">fluid simulator</a> can be used for simulating liquids, like water hitting a cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> It uses the <a href="/wiki/Lattice_Boltzmann_methods" title="Lattice Boltzmann methods">Lattice Boltzmann methods</a> to simulate the fluids and allows for lots of adjusting of the amount of particles and the resolution.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Particle_fluid_simulation">Particle fluid simulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Particle fluid simulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The particle physics fluid simulation creates particles that follow the <a href="/wiki/Smoothed-particle_hydrodynamics" title="Smoothed-particle hydrodynamics">Smoothed-particle hydrodynamics</a> method.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stucco-blendergame.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="996" data-file-width="1680" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Stucco-blendergame.jpg/250px-Stucco-blendergame.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Stucco-blendergame.jpg/375px-Stucco-blendergame.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Stucco-blendergame.jpg/500px-Stucco-blendergame.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stucco-blendergame.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Game engine <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GLSL" title="GLSL">GLSL</a> materials</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since the opening of the source, Blender has experienced significant <a href="/wiki/Code_refactoring" title="Code refactoring">refactoring</a> of the initial codebase and major additions to its feature set.</p>
<p>Improvements include an animation system refresh;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> a stack-based modifier system;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> an updated particle system<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> (which can also be used to simulate hair and fur); fluid dynamics; soft-body dynamics; GLSL shaders support<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> in the game engine; advanced UV unwrapping;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> a fully recoded render pipeline, allowing separate render passes and "render to texture"; node-based material editing and compositing; and projection painting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>Part of these developments were fostered by <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Google_Summer_of_Code" title="Google Summer of Code">Summer of Code</a> program, in which the Blender Foundation has participated since 2005.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Support">Support</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Support">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Blender is extensively documented on its website,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> with the rest of the support provided via community tutorials and discussion forums on the Internet. The Blender Network provides support and social services for Blender Professionals. Additionally, <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> is known to have a great many video tutorials available for either Blender amateurs or professionals at no cost.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Use_in_the_media_industry">Use in the media industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Use in the media industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Blender started out as an inhouse tool for a Dutch commercial animation company NeoGeo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Blender has been used for television commercials in several parts of the world including <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>Blender is used by <i><a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a></i> for publicly available 3D models. Many 3D models on NASAs 3D resources page are in a native .blend format.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Experience_curiosity1.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1920" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Experience_curiosity1.png/220px-Experience_curiosity1.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Experience_curiosity1.png/330px-Experience_curiosity1.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Experience_curiosity1.png/440px-Experience_curiosity1.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Experience_curiosity1.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Experience_Curiosity" title="Experience Curiosity">Experience Curiosity</a>: taking a <a href="/wiki/Selfie" title="Selfie">Selfie</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>NASA also used Blender and <a href="/wiki/Blend4Web" title="Blend4Web">Blend4Web</a> to develop an interactive web application to celebrate the 3rd anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Curiosity_(rover)" title="Curiosity (rover)">Curiosity rover</a> landing on <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa-press-release_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-nasa-press-release-57">[57]</a></sup> This app<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-curiosity-app_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-curiosity-app-58">[58]</a></sup> makes it possible to operate the rover, control its cameras and the <a href="/wiki/Robotic_arm" title="Robotic arm">robotic arm</a> and reproduces some of the prominent events of the <a href="/wiki/Mars_Science_Laboratory" title="Mars Science Laboratory">Mars Science Laboratory</a> mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blend4web-blog-nasa_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-blend4web-blog-nasa-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-technology-org-nasa-webapp_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-technology-org-nasa-webapp-60">[60]</a></sup> The application was presented at the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/WebGL" title="WebGL">WebGL</a> section on <a href="/wiki/SIGGRAPH" title="SIGGRAPH">SIGGRAPH</a> 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-khronos-events-2015-SIGGRAPH_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-khronos-events-2015-SIGGRAPH-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first large professional project that used Blender was <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_2" title="Spider-Man 2">Spider-Man 2</a></i>, where it was primarily used to create <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animatic" title="Animatic">animatics</a> and pre-visualizations for the <a href="/wiki/Storyboard" title="Storyboard">storyboard</a> department.</p>
<dl>
<dd>
<dl>
<dd><i>As an animatic artist working in the storyboard department of Spider-Man 2, I used Blender<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s 3D modeling and character animation tools to enhance the storyboards, re-creating sets and props, and putting into motion action and camera moves in 3D space to help make <a href="/wiki/Sam_Raimi" title="Sam Raimi">Sam Raimi<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s</a> vision as clear to other departments as possible.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> – Anthony Zierhut,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Animatic Artist, Los Angeles.</dd>
</dl>
</dd>
</dl>
<p>The French-language film <i><a href="/wiki/Friday_or_Another_Day" title="Friday or Another Day">Friday or Another Day</a></i> (<i><a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vendredi_ou_un_autre_jour" title="fr:Vendredi ou un autre jour">Vendredi ou un autre jour</a></i>) was the first 35 mm feature film to use Blender for all the special effects, made on Linux workstations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> It won a prize at the <a href="/wiki/Locarno_International_Film_Festival" title="Locarno International Film Festival">Locarno International Film Festival</a>. The special effects were by Digital Graphics<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> of Belgium.</p>
<p>Blender has also been used for shows on the <a href="/wiki/History_(U.S._TV_channel)" title="History (U.S. TV channel)">History Channel</a>, alongside many other professional 3D graphics programs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tomm_Moore" title="Tomm Moore">Tomm Moore</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Secret_of_Kells" title="The Secret of Kells">The Secret of Kells</a></i>, which was partly produced in Blender by the Belgian studio Digital Graphics, has been nominated for an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Oscar</a> in the category "<a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Animated_Feature" title="Academy Award for Best Animated Feature">Best Animated Feature Film</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Plum%C3%ADferos" title="Plumíferos">Plumíferos</a></i>, a commercial animated feature film created entirely in Blender,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> was premiered in February 2010 in Argentina. Its main characters are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anthropomorphic" title="Anthropomorphic">anthropomorphic</a> <a href="/wiki/Talking_animal" title="Talking animal">talking animals</a>.</p>
<p>Special effects for <a href="/wiki/The_Beginning_(Red_Dwarf)" title="The Beginning (Red Dwarf)">episode 6</a> of <a href="/wiki/Red_Dwarf" title="Red Dwarf">Red Dwarf</a> season X were confirmed being created using Blender by half of Gecko Animation, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Simonds&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ben Simonds (page does not exist)">Ben Simonds</a>. The company responsible for the special effects, Gecko Animation, uses Blender for multiple projects, including Red Dwarf.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The episode screened in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Blender was used for both CGI and compositing for the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Hardcore_Henry" title="Hardcore Henry">Hardcore Henry</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Open_projects">Open projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Open projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:154px;max-width:154px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Big_buck_bunny_poster_big.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2122" data-file-width="1500" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Big_buck_bunny_poster_big.jpg/150px-Big_buck_bunny_poster_big.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Big_buck_bunny_poster_big.jpg/225px-Big_buck_bunny_poster_big.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Big_buck_bunny_poster_big.jpg/300px-Big_buck_bunny_poster_big.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><i>Big Buck Bunny</i> poster</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sintel_poster.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="905" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Sintel_poster.jpg/150px-Sintel_poster.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Sintel_poster.jpg/225px-Sintel_poster.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Sintel_poster.jpg/300px-Sintel_poster.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div>

</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tos-poster.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="2700" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Tos-poster.png/150px-Tos-poster.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Tos-poster.png/225px-Tos-poster.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Tos-poster.png/300px-Tos-poster.png 2x" width="150"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><i>Tears of Steel</i> promotional poster</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Every 1–2 years the Blender Foundation announces a new creative project to help drive innovation in Blender.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elephants_Dream_.28Open_Movie_Project:_Orange.29"><i>Elephants Dream</i> (Open Movie Project: Orange)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Elephants Dream (Open Movie Project: Orange)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Elephants_Dream" title="Elephants Dream">Elephants Dream</a></div>
<p>In September 2005, some of the most notable Blender artists and developers began working on a short film using primarily <a href="/wiki/Free_software" title="Free software">free software</a>, in an initiative known as the Orange Movie Project hosted by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Netherlands_Media_Art_Institute_(NIMk)" title="Netherlands Media Art Institute (NIMk)">Netherlands Media Art Institute (NIMk)</a>. The resulting film, <i>Elephants Dream</i>, premiered on March 24, 2006. In response to the success of <i>Elephants Dream</i>, the Blender Foundation founded the Blender Institute to do additional projects with two announced projects: <i><a href="/wiki/Big_Buck_Bunny" title="Big Buck Bunny">Big Buck Bunny</a></i>, also known as "Project Peach" (a 'furry and funny' short open animated film project) and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yo_Frankie" title="Yo Frankie">Yo Frankie</a></i>, also known as Project Apricot (an open game in collaboration with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CrystalSpace" title="CrystalSpace">CrystalSpace</a> that reused some of the assets created during Project Peach). This has later made its way to <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_3DS" title="Nintendo 3DS">Nintendo 3DS</a>'s Nintendo Video between the years 2012 and 2013.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Big_Buck_Bunny_.28Open_Movie_Project:_Peach.29"><i>Big Buck Bunny</i> (Open Movie Project: Peach)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Big Buck Bunny (Open Movie Project: Peach)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Big_Buck_Bunny" title="Big Buck Bunny">Big Buck Bunny</a></div>
<p>On October 1, 2007, a new team started working on a second open project, "Peach", for the production of the short movie <i>Big Buck Bunny</i>. This time, however, the creative concept was totally different. Instead of the deep and mystical style of <i>Elephants Dream</i>, things are more "funny and furry" according to the official site.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The movie had its premiere on April 10, 2008.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Yo_Frankie.21_.28Open_Game_Project:_Apricot.29"><i>Yo Frankie!</i> (Open Game Project: Apricot)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Yo Frankie! (Open Game Project: Apricot)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Yo_Frankie!" title="Yo Frankie!">Yo Frankie!</a></div>
<p>"Apricot" is a project for production of a game based on the universe and characters of the Peach movie (<i><a href="/wiki/Big_Buck_Bunny" title="Big Buck Bunny">Big Buck Bunny</a></i>) using <a href="/wiki/Free_software" title="Free software">free software</a>. The game is titled <i>Yo Frankie</i>. The project started February 1, 2008, and development was completed at the end of July 2008. A finalized product was expected at the end of August; however, the release was delayed. The game was released on December 9, 2008, under either the <a href="/wiki/GNU_General_Public_License" title="GNU General Public License">GNU GPL</a> or <a href="/wiki/GNU_Lesser_General_Public_License" title="GNU Lesser General Public License">LGPL</a>, with all content being licensed under <a href="/wiki/Creative_Commons" title="Creative Commons">Creative Commons</a> Attribution 3.0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-about-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sintel_.28Open_Movie_Project:_Durian.29"><i>Sintel</i> (Open Movie Project: Durian)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Sintel (Open Movie Project: Durian)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sintel" title="Sintel">Sintel</a></div>
<p>The Blender Foundation's Project Durian<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> (in keeping with the tradition of fruits as code names) was this time chosen to make a <a href="/wiki/Fantasy" title="Fantasy">fantasy</a> action epic of about twelve minutes in length,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> starring a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teenager" title="Teenager">teenage</a> girl and a young <a href="/wiki/Dragon" title="Dragon">dragon</a> as the main characters. The film premiered online on September 30, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> A game based on <i>Sintel</i> was officially announced on Blenderartists.org on May 12, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many of the new features integrated into Blender 2.5 and beyond were a direct result of Project Durian.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tears_of_Steel_.28Open_Movie_Project:_Mango.29"><i>Tears of Steel</i> (Open Movie Project: Mango)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Tears of Steel (Open Movie Project: Mango)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tears_of_Steel" title="Tears of Steel">Tears of Steel</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tears_of_Steel_frame_08_4a.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="3840" height="92" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Tears_of_Steel_frame_08_4a.jpg/220px-Tears_of_Steel_frame_08_4a.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Tears_of_Steel_frame_08_4a.jpg/330px-Tears_of_Steel_frame_08_4a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Tears_of_Steel_frame_08_4a.jpg/440px-Tears_of_Steel_frame_08_4a.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tears_of_Steel_frame_08_4a.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Derek_de_Lint" title="Derek de Lint">Derek de Lint</a> in a scene from <i>Tears of Steel</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On October 2, 2011, the fourth open movie project, codenamed "Mango", was announced by the <a href="/wiki/Blender_Foundation" title="Blender Foundation">Blender Foundation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-roosendaal1_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-roosendaal1-81">[81]</a></sup> A team of artists assembled using an open call of community participation. It is the first Blender open movie to use live action as well as CG.</p>
<p>Filming for Mango started on May 7, 2012, and the movie was released on September 26, 2012. As with the previous films, all footage, scenes and models were made available under a <a href="/wiki/Free_content" title="Free content">free content</a> compliant <a href="/wiki/Creative_Commons" title="Creative Commons">Creative Commons</a> license.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-roosendaal1_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-roosendaal1-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the film's press release, "The film's premise is about a group of warriors and scientists, who gather at the '<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oude_Kerk_(Amsterdam)" title="Oude Kerk (Amsterdam)">Oude Kerk</a>' in Amsterdam to stage a crucial event from the past, in a desperate attempt to rescue the world from destructive robots."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cosmos_Laundromat_.28Open_Movie_Project:_Gooseberry.29"><i>Cosmos Laundromat</i> (Open Movie Project: Gooseberry)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Cosmos Laundromat (Open Movie Project: Gooseberry)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cosmos_Laundromat" title="Cosmos Laundromat">Cosmos Laundromat</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

<i>Cosmos Laundromat</i> – First Cycle</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On January 10, 2011, Ton Roosendaal announced that the fifth open movie project would be codenamed "Gooseberry" and that its goal would be to produce a feature-length animated film. He speculated that production would begin sometime between 2012 and 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The film was to be written and produced by a coalition of international animation studios. The studio lineup was announced on January 28, 2014,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> and production began soon thereafter. As of March 2014, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moodboard" title="Moodboard">moodboard</a> had been constructed<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> and development goals had been set. The initial ten minute pilot was released on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> on August 10, 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> It won the <a href="/wiki/SIGGRAPH" title="SIGGRAPH">SIGGRAPH</a> 2016 Computer Animation Festival Jury's Choice award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Online_services">Online services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Online services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Blender_Cloud">Blender Cloud</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Blender Cloud">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <b>Blender Cloud</b> platform, launched in March 2014 and operated by the Blender Institute, is a subscription-based <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud computing</a> platform and Blender client add-on which provides hosting and synchronization for backed-up animation project files.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> It was launched to promote and fundraise for <i>Project: Gooseberry</i>, and is intended to replace the selling of DVDs by the Blender Foundation with a subscription-based model for file hosting, asset sharing and collaboration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> A feature of the Blender Cloud is <b>Blender Sync</b>, which provides synchronization between Blender clients for file changes, user preferences and other features.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Blender_ID">Blender ID</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Blender_(software)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Blender ID">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <b>Blender ID</b> is a unified login for Blender software and service users, providing a login for Blender Cloud, the Blender Store, the Blender Conference, Blender Network, Blender Development Fund and the Blender Foundation Certified Trainer Program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
